Andersen</title><content type='html'>Once again I've been scooped by "&lt;a href="https://www.blogger.com/profile/06787762757245289307"&gt;DaShark&lt;/a&gt;", who beat me to the punch in pointing out Julie Andersen's hypocrisy in her latest &lt;a href="https://www.facebook.com/thesharkangels/videos/991799084166213/"&gt;post&lt;/a&gt;, telling us to "Do as I say and not as I do". I other words he pointed out what a complete hypocrite this "Shark Angel" and "shark expert" really is. She once again showed that she is much more interested in promoting herself, rather than shark conservation.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Read "&lt;a href="https://www.blogger.com/profile/06787762757245289307"&gt;DaShark's&lt;/a&gt;" blog &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/2015/06/andersen-at-it-again.html"&gt;here &lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Back in 2013 Julie wrote an &lt;a href="http://www.scubadiving.com/photos/ask-expert-it-ok-touch-shark?src=SOC&amp;amp;dom=fb"&gt;article&lt;/a&gt; for "&lt;a href="http://www.scubadiving.com/"&gt;SCUBA Diving&lt;/a&gt;" where she wrote. &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"T&lt;span style="line-height: 20px;"&gt;he topic of touching &lt;a href="http://www.scubadiving.com/photos/divers-guide-marine-life-sharks" target="_blank"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt; can spark heated debates. It’s an inner turmoil I wrestle with often,  having spent hundreds of hours underwater with them. A quick Google  search reveals many images in which I am brazenly touching sharks. Yes,  it is something I did (and often still am tempted to do), but it is  something I don’t encourage. In fact, just the opposite."&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have to admit, that I did have a problem with her stand, because she gained her fame by touching and riding sharks and once she had that name recognition, she didn't want others to get in on the act and compete with her for sponsorships, money and fame. Ok, we all make mistakes and who hasn't done something we are not proud  of? I thought: "at least she admits that she did something that  wasn't good and is changing".&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Skip a couple of years and &lt;a href="https://www.facebook.com/thesharkangels/videos/991799084166213/"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt; is her latest post on&amp;nbsp; &lt;a data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;k&amp;quot;}" data-gt="{&amp;quot;entity_id&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;208271845852278&amp;quot;,&amp;quot;entity_path&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;WebPhotoPermalinkController&amp;quot;}" data-hovercard="/ajax/hovercard/page.php?id=208271845852278" href="https://www.facebook.com/thesharkangels?fref=photo"&gt;"Shark Angels&lt;/a&gt;"&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;It's time to change your perspective. &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span class="fbPhotosPhotoCaption" data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;*G&amp;quot;,&amp;quot;type&amp;quot;:45}" id="fbPhotoPageCaption" tabindex="0"&gt;&lt;span class="hasCaption"&gt; &lt;br /&gt; Watch this stunning new video from &lt;a data-gt="{&amp;quot;entity_id&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;116337731749935&amp;quot;,&amp;quot;entity_path&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;WebPhotoPermalinkController&amp;quot;}" data-hovercard="/ajax/hovercard/page.php?id=116337731749935&amp;amp;extragetparams=%7B%22directed_target_id%22%3A0%7D" href="https://www.facebook.com/BuiltByWildman"&gt;Built By Wildman&lt;/a&gt; featuring founder &lt;a data-gt="{&amp;quot;entity_id&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;154668527926558&amp;quot;,&amp;quot;entity_path&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;WebPhotoPermalinkController&amp;quot;}" data-hovercard="/ajax/hovercard/page.php?id=154668527926558&amp;amp;extragetparams=%7B%22directed_target_id%22%3A0%7D" href="https://www.facebook.com/juliesharkangel"&gt;Julie Andersen&lt;/a&gt; showing the world sharks aren't what they seem. Apparently his feelings are hurt, that a blog about celebrities at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt; was not about him.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;He writes: &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".2b.1:$comment10153287938456419:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0"&gt;&lt;a class=" UFICommentActorName" data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;;&amp;quot;}" data-hovercard="/ajax/hovercard/hovercard.php?id=192917914087364&amp;amp;extragetparams=%7B%22hc_location%22%3A%22ufi%22%7D" data-reactid=".2b.1:$comment10153287938456419:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0.0" dir="ltr" href="https://www.facebook.com/CHRISFISCHEROCEARCH" id="js_15"&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".2b.1:$comment10153287938456419:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.0.0.0"&gt;Chris Fischer&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".2b.1:$comment10153287938456419:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1"&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".2b.1:$comment10153287938456419:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.0"&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" data-reactid=".2b.1:$comment10153287938456419:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body"&gt;&lt;span class="UFICommentBody" data-reactid=".2b.1:$comment10153287938456419:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body.0"&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".2b.1:$comment10153287938456419:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body.0.0"&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".2b.1:$comment10153287938456419:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body.0.0.$text0:0:$0:0"&gt;Thrilled you are a fan of &lt;/span&gt;&lt;a class="profileLink" data-hovercard="/ajax/hovercard/hovercard.php?id=249354835166&amp;amp;extragetparams=%7B%22hc_location%22%3A%22ufi%22%7D" data-reactid=".2b.1:$comment10153287938456419:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body.0.0.$range0:0" dir="ltr" href="https://www.facebook.com/OCEARCH?hc_location=ufi" id="js_12" target="_blank"&gt;OCEARCH&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".2b.1:$comment10153287938456419:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body.0.0.$end:0:$0:0"&gt; work.  My wife and I personally funded the expedition that tagged  Bruce.  Amusing how you fail to mention the crew and capacity that  created the data you feel is so important. Domeier simply stepped down  tagged the sha&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".2b.1:$comment10153287938456419:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body.0.3"&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".2b.1:$comment10153287938456419:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body.0.3.0"&gt;&lt;span data-reactid=".2b.1:$comment10153287938456419:0.0.$right.0.$left.0.0.1.$comment-body.0.3.0.$end:0:$0:0"&gt;rk  then got out of the way.  The crew did everything else to safely tag  and release Bruce! Additionally, you know the sharks are returning now  after shedding the tags with their fins healed up doing well yet you  continue to let the others bash...  We have spoken to the researchers  using the 1 bolt method.. they are uncertain how well it's going to work  long term as well the increase in bio-fouling from all the different  cracks and crevices created by the mount. We have requested Wildlife  Computers to try to design a modified mounting system... But as you  already know, this is not required as they shed the tags after 5yrs or  so and heal up nicely.  You should watch Mary Lee on the Global Shark  Tracker.  She is getting ready to repeat the success we had at Guadalupe  Island by documenting the 1st full female mature white shark migration  in the N Atlantic. Soon we will know where they are mating/birthing  etc... just like out where you profit from cage diving at GI.  I figure  our work is the best chance you got at being able to own a  multi-generational business.  Acting like we don't exist is amateurish  and rude.  We are currently on Expedition off West Australia where we  have tagged 20 Tiger Sharks to solve the same puzzle as we did in GI to  create a future for sharks here.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Please forgive me Chris, I had no idea that I would hurt your feelings by writing about a celebrity without mentioning you. How rude of me. So since your feelings are hurt by me not mentioning you, let me respond to what you are saying.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1. I don't quite get why you think I'm a fan of OCEARCH &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2. Your wife and you financed the expedition that tagged Bruce. I never wrote anything about who financed that expedition, or why that is even relevant, but since you claim you did, let me also state what Dr. Domeier said about that.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;From &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/2013/04/fischer-reality-check-comments-by-dr.html"&gt;http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/2013/04/fischer-reality-check-comments-by-dr.html&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Yes, he paid for 2 trips to Guadalupe, but  then struck a TV deal that allowed him to recoup those costs as he was  getting $400K/episode.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;i&gt;We were able to make multiple episodes from a  single trip. Furthermore, I tapped two other private foundations to  help pay for the tags and research; financial support that he never  acknowledges. Fischer was fairly paid for all of the work we did  together… this was not a huge philanthropic venture. On the contrary, he  made it clear: “no cameras no trips.” The huge $$ figure he throws  around must be for the entire operating cost of his ship and production  company for each year he was making these television shows. But that’s  not a fair way to account for the actual cost of the research (a  fraction of the yearly operating budgets were due to the handful of  research trips)… and he never discusses the INCOME. Any real accountant  would tally just the costs of the specific trips… or think like this:  what would it cost to charter a vessel for each research trip, and then  subtract the income! Perhaps he took a loss, I don’t know; my  organization took a financial loss… but no way did either of us wrack up  losses in the millions. &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;Read more of &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/about-us/"&gt;Dr. Domeier's&lt;/a&gt; comments &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/2013/04/fischer-reality-check-comments-by-dr.html"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3. Domeier simply stepped down, tagged the shark and then got away?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;OK, and the research paper appeared out of thin air?&amp;nbsp;My advise to you would be this. Make it about the sharks instead of  about you. You and I are not important, saving the sharks is. Your need  to be seen as a shark expert is not important. You provide a platform  for the researchers, they are the experts. Why do you feel the need to  belittle what they do? Catching and tagging the sharks is a means to an  end. The end is the research and that is what the researchers do. For example, I  collect photos at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt; for &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/about-us/"&gt;Nicole Nasby-Lucas&lt;/a&gt;. She is doing  the research for the photo ID's. I have nothing to do with that. If  someone mentions her research, there is no need for them to say anything  about me, or anyone else who gave her the pictures.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4. You write that I know that Bruce has been returning safely to Guadalupe every year. Ah, why do you think I don't know that? I have always stated that the second generation tags, that Bruce and Bite Face were fitted with, have fallen off and there is little damage to their fins. I even put a picture of Bruce into the blog, that shows him after he lost the transmitter.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-Vy1lMmuOXxA/VUT26lRWVWI/AAAAAAAABZU/IbjpvZMgNLU/s1600/Bruce%2Bhealed.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="187" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-Vy1lMmuOXxA/VUT26lRWVWI/AAAAAAAABZU/IbjpvZMgNLU/s400/Bruce%2Bhealed.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;5. I let others bash you? Well, for one, how can I control what others do? Actually, I'm trying to tell others to &lt;a href="http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/04/how-do-you-get-taken-seriously-as.html"&gt;keep an open mind&lt;/a&gt;. I wrote the following in my &lt;a href="http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2014/02/how-can-you-safe-sharks.html"&gt;blog&lt;/a&gt; &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;"&lt;i&gt;All the tagging done in a year, may cause harm to a few  hundred sharks. Again, that's a few hundred, vs. 30-100 MILLION sharks  killed annually.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If the protests succeed and there is no more tagging, at best we could  save a few sharks every year and make life easier (no tags, no deformed  dorsal fin etc.) for a few more. On the other hand, we could also loose  valuable data, that may help save sharks. You decide, if it is  worthwhile to focus on this. Personally I think we need to weigh the  importance of the data collected against the potential harm to the  sharks."&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My beef with you has always been about lifting the sharks out of the  water and not improving your methods. It's no longer necessary to lift  them out, as &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/about-us/"&gt;Dr. Domeier&lt;/a&gt; has shown. I have defended your early work by  saying that the Wright brothers didn't invent an A380 either. Pictures like this should only come from the past by now.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="https://scontent-lax.xx.fbcdn.net/hphotos-xpa1/t31.0-8/11181225_10155421112060167_5905106080001109334_o.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="266" src="https://scontent-lax.xx.fbcdn.net/hphotos-xpa1/t31.0-8/11181225_10155421112060167_5905106080001109334_o.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Do you have any idea how many people bash me, for not outright condemning anything you do? I hurt your feelings by not defending everything you do and mentioning your name every time I write about something that was connected to you. The blog you are referring to in your comment was about the real celebrities at Guadalupe Island, the sharks, not you.&amp;nbsp;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;5. I am acting like you don't exist? How can you say I act like you don't exist and on the other hand criticize what I say about you?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you start to improve your methods of catching sharks and attaching the transmitters, I will give you credit for that.&amp;nbsp; If you start giving some credit to the researchers who are doing the actual studies, instead of promoting yourself as the shark expert, I promise to write an entire blog, promoting the new and improved Chris Fischer.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. Sharks can SAVE lives!</title><content type='html'>We are used to the media using sensationalistic headlines when covering anything to do with sharks. "Jaws" "Monster" "Beast" "Mankiller" etc. are no unusual terms in those headlines.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is the second time this year that we have to give &lt;a href="http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/04/shark-attacks-and-media.html"&gt;kudos to a news&lt;/a&gt;&lt;a href="https://www.blogger.com/null"&gt; outlet&lt;/a&gt;. The &lt;a href="http://www.dailymail.co.uk/"&gt;Daily Mail&lt;/a&gt; has a headline that says: &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;Forget Jaws! Sharks can SAVE lives! &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;You read that right, no scare tactic, no monsters, .... actually OK, they did mention monsters, but not the way we are used to either. The second part of their headline reads: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;We think of them as monsters, but a new documentary reveals they could help us fight cancer and Alzheimer's&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Hey, they even use a cool picture of one of "our" &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;great white sharks&lt;/a&gt;. This is "Johnny"!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://i.dailymail.co.uk/i/pix/2015/04/30/13/2818149B00000578-3062503-image-m-26_1430397243793.jpg" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://i.dailymail.co.uk/i/pix/2015/04/30/13/2818149B00000578-3062503-image-m-26_1430397243793.jpg" height="290" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://i.dailymail.co.uk/i/pix/2015/04/30/13/2818149B00000578-3062503-image-m-26_1430397243793.jpg"&gt;source&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;They are acknowledging how sharks are normally portrayed. &lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;Der-dum...  der-dum... der, der, der, der, der, der... Mention sharks and, thanks  to Steven Spielberg’s 1975 blockbuster Jaws, those suspenseful notes of  impending attack are, for most, what springs immediately to mind.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="articleWide cleared"&gt;&lt;div class="alpha"&gt;&lt;div class="article-text wide" id="js-article-text"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="background-color: white;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div class="mol-para-with-font"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="background-color: white;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;The  movie masterpiece, which is 40 years old this summer, led to many a  phobia, but according to a new three-part BBC1 documentary Shark, its  toothy star isn’t that terrifying in real-life.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="mol-para-with-font"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="background-color: white;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&amp;nbsp; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="mol-para-with-font"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="background-color: white;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;The article&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt; is talking about &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="background-color: white;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="background-color: white;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;a documentary series &lt;a href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/programmes/p02n7s0d"&gt;"Sharks"&lt;/a&gt;, the &lt;a href="http://www.bbc.com/"&gt;BBC&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt; has produced and&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt; it covers a lot of different sides of sharks. They write about the scientific discoveries we made that could mean sharks can help with various human diseases, like Alzheimer's. It is also covering a bunch of different shark species and is giving some very good information on sharks.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="mol-para-with-font"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="mol-para-with-font"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="background-color: white;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;You can read the entire article here: &lt;a href="http://www.dailymail.co.uk/femail/article-3062503/Forget-Jaws-Sharks-SAVE-lives-think-monsters-new-documentary-reveals-help-fight-cancer-Alzheimer-s.html?"&gt;&lt;i&gt;http://www.dailymail.co.uk/femail/article-3062503/Forget-Jaws-Sharks-SAVE-lives-think-monsters-new-documentary-reveals-help-fight-cancer-Alzheimer-s.html?&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="background-color: white;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;b&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Of course we also want to give kudos to the &lt;a href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/programmes/p02n7s0d"&gt;BBC&lt;/a&gt;, which seems to be one of the few television outlets that are still producing quality shark documentaries, a far cry from the crap that &lt;a href="http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/04/shark-documentary-causing-problems-in.html"&gt;ABC4 and Jeff Kurr&lt;/a&gt;, are &lt;a href="http://www.ew.com/article/2014/08/12/shark-week-lair-mega-shark"&gt;producing for the discovery channel&lt;/a&gt;. Check out BBC's "Shark" website here: &lt;a href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/programmes/p02n7s0d"&gt;http://www.bbc.co.uk/programmes/p02n7s0d&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let's go &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark diving!&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver &lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. You can reach us directly at staff@sharkdiver.com.</content><link rel='replies' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/feeds/3660871889900584769/comments/default' title='Post Comments'/><link rel='replies' type='text/html' href='https://www.blogger.com/comment.g?blogID=370711998877298323&amp;postID=3660871889900584769' title='0 Comments'/><link rel='edit' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/3660871889900584769'/><link rel='self' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/3660871889900584769'/><link rel='alternate' type='text/html' href='http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/05/forget-jaws-sharks-can-save-lives.html' title='Forget Jaws! Sharks can SAVE lives!'/><author><name>Shark Diver</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/107965598445039841723</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='32' height='32' src='//lh5.googleusercontent.com/-acNbaifFSTQ/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAB_A/inqVjDI-1J8/s32-c/photo.jpg'/></author><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-524191328074989946</id><published>2015-05-02T09:26:00.002-07:00</published><updated>2015-05-02T09:26:57.102-07:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark diver'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='cage diving'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='swimming with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='cage diving with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='guadalupe island'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><title type='text'>Celebrities at Guadalupe Island</title><content type='html'>The world is full of celebrities, but how often do you actually get to meet them and spend some quality time with them?&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;Over the past 14 years, I've been privileged to do just that. I've met many stars of film and TV at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe Island.&lt;/a&gt; Stars like the incomparable "Shredder" "Bruce" "Jaques" "Lucy" "Scarboard" etc. All of those sharks have been featured in countless shark week episodes and their pictures are all over the internet. They truly are the rock-stars of Guadalupe Island.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have talked about "Shredder" &lt;a href="http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/01/the-baddest-shark-at-isla-guadalupe.html"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt; and "Chugey's" amazing recovery from a huge bite &lt;a href="http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2013/08/how-fast-do-great-white-sharks-heal.html"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2014/09/chugey-is-back-at-guadalupe.html"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Today I want to introduce you to  "Bruce", another regular at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;. Bruce has been around since we started &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark diving&lt;/a&gt; at Guadalupe. When we first encountered him, he was just a "little" teenager, probably not much longer than 11-12'. Of course we had no idea that we would see him year after year and that he would grow into one of the larger males at the Island. He is now on the north side of 16' and one of the dominant shark at the site.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-c4zd69DtLQM/VPX6VvjhQ1I/AAAAAAAABTQ/yQk49u9d4NI/s1600/shark%2Bsmile.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-c4zd69DtLQM/VPX6VvjhQ1I/AAAAAAAABTQ/yQk49u9d4NI/s1600/shark%2Bsmile.jpg" height="265" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;Bruce saying hello to Whitney, one of our divers!&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Bruce is also the shark who got me interested in shark research. I have to admit, that reading scientific papers held about as much excitement to me as watching grass grow. It simply wasn't my thing. When &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/about-us/"&gt;Dr. Domeier&lt;/a&gt; tagged Bruce with a satellite transmitter and used some of the data it produced for his paper on white shark migration, &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/about-us/"&gt;Nicole Nasby-Lucas&lt;/a&gt;, who works with &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/about-us/"&gt;Dr. Domeier&lt;/a&gt; and is responsible for the &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/white-shark/"&gt;Guadalupe photo ID database&lt;/a&gt;, gave me a copy of the research paper. I started reading it, and realized that this paper was not just a research paper, but more like Bruce's travel journal. It was exciting to find out where he was going, when not at Guadalupe and what he was doing. Who knew that he was vacationing near Hawaii?! I mean, who wouldn't want to vacation there?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Even though he is one of the more mellow &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt; around, being a &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;great white shark&lt;/a&gt; and male, Bruce was not averse to a little fighting here and there. I remember one particular morning. I was just getting into the cages to sort out all the regulators, when I noticed some movement behind me. I turned and saw Bruce who looked me straight into the eyes. He sported a huge bite injury, just in front of his gills, with a hole that let me look straight through it and out his mouth. The amazing thing was, it didn't seem to bother him. He just kept swimming around and stayed active, like nothing had happened.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-9WwfkWgjaW8/VUT2u0ZpXFI/AAAAAAAABZI/kSJ2hALd0fg/s1600/Bruce%2Bwith%2Bbite.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-9WwfkWgjaW8/VUT2u0ZpXFI/AAAAAAAABZI/kSJ2hALd0fg/s1600/Bruce%2Bwith%2Bbite.jpg" height="285" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;Bruce about a week after the bite.&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Just like Chugey, when he came back the following year, his wound was closed and there was barely a scar to indicate that he was ever injured.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-Vy1lMmuOXxA/VUT26lRWVWI/AAAAAAAABZQ/33Vuu0KI8_M/s1600/Bruce%2Bhealed.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-Vy1lMmuOXxA/VUT26lRWVWI/AAAAAAAABZQ/33Vuu0KI8_M/s1600/Bruce%2Bhealed.jpg" height="187" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;Bruce with his closed bite injury.&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So that is Bruce.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Since we started shark diving at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;, we have met over 160 different individual &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt;. Who is going to be back this year? Who is going to make their first appearance? Come join us and find out! This is your chance to meet these celebrities up close and personal. They do pose for pictures with you! Next time you watch shark week, you can say, "Hey, I know that guy!"&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;We run our trips from August through November and have a few spaces left for this coming season. We even have a couple of spaces open on our research trip on November 11. On that trip you'll get to meet the researcher who knows all about those sharks, &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/about-us/"&gt;Nicole Nasby-Lucas&lt;/a&gt;, along with all the rock-star &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;white sharks&lt;/a&gt; of &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;. Call us at 619.887.4275 or email staff@sharkdiver.com for more information.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let's go &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark diving&lt;/a&gt;!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. width='72'/><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-735291271065238676</id><published>2015-05-01T13:00:00.003-07:00</published><updated>2015-05-01T13:00:34.770-07:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='florida shark fishing'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark diver'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='killing sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='conservation'/><title type='text'>Sharks need your help in Florida!</title><content type='html'>&lt;a href="https://www.blogger.com/profile/06787762757245289307"&gt;DaShark&lt;/a&gt;, through his &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/"&gt;blog&lt;/a&gt;, just made me aware of something that is &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/2015/05/targeting-pregnant-sharks-in-florida.html"&gt;happening in Florida right now.&lt;/a&gt; Apparently shore fishermen are (legally) fishing for pregnant bull sharks. A lot of those sharks, even if released will die, along with their pups. This is nothing new, it's been going on for &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/2010/04/left-to-die.html"&gt;years&lt;/a&gt;. &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://40.media.tumblr.com/tumblr_ljb9ukIUea1qfdn20o1_1280.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://40.media.tumblr.com/tumblr_ljb9ukIUea1qfdn20o1_1280.jpg" height="308" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://40.media.tumblr.com/tumblr_ljb9ukIUea1qfdn20o1_1280.jpg"&gt;source&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;I know a lot of you who are reading this, are living in Florida. If you want to do something to help those sharks, this is your chance. Talk to your legislators, educate those fishermen, find out what groups are already working there and how you can help. &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;According to the &lt;a href="http://www.keysnet.com/"&gt;Keys Info Net&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Everglades National Park managers have the ability to declare an  emergency rule to restrict access when protected species are found  breeding in an area,"&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;So call or write the Everglades National Park manager. Read Key Info Net's entire article&amp;nbsp; &lt;a href="http://www.keysnet.com/2015/04/29/502450_dying-sharks-off-lower-matecumbe.html?rh=1"&gt;http://www.keysnet.com/2015/04/29/502450_dying-sharks-off-lower-matecumbe.html?rh=1&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Pupping season is right now! The &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt; need your help, do what you can! If you can, go to that beach at night and talk to the fishermen, let them know, why it is not a good idea to target those sharks. Remember, you will have a better chance of convincing them, if you are polite. &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver &lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. You can reach us directly at staff@sharkdiver.com.</content><link rel='replies' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/feeds/735291271065238676/comments/default' title='Post Comments'/><link rel='replies' type='text/html' href='https://www.blogger.com/comment.g?blogID=370711998877298323&amp;postID=735291271065238676' title='0 Comments'/><link rel='edit' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/735291271065238676'/><link rel='self' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/735291271065238676'/><link rel='alternate' type='text/html' href='http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/05/sharks-need-your-help-in-florida.html' title='Sharks need your help in Florida!'/><author><name>Shark Diver</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/107965598445039841723</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='32' height='32' src='//lh5.googleusercontent.com/-acNbaifFSTQ/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAB_A/inqVjDI-1J8/s32-c/photo.jpg'/></author><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-4897312468383779872</id><published>2015-04-27T09:30:00.000-07:00</published><updated>2015-04-27T09:32:35.922-07:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='cage diving with great white sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark conservation'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='swimming with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='cage diving with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='guadalupe island'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><title type='text'>Amazing!</title><content type='html'>I've been diving with the great white sharks at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/guadalupe-island/"&gt;Isla Guadalupe&lt;/a&gt; for 13 years now. Over time, I've come to marvel at the &lt;a href="http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2013/08/how-fast-do-great-white-sharks-heal.html"&gt;healing ability&lt;/a&gt; of the sharks, the mysteries of their migration, their distinctly  different personalities and most of all, and this is what blows my mind,  the fact that I can go to Guadalupe and know that I will see, not just  any great white shark, but a particular individual great white shark.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Mw5BoT_RGOg/UiEE9Oj_EgI/AAAAAAAAAOk/B0lbnmYNLak/s1600/%2356.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Mw5BoT_RGOg/UiEE9Oj_EgI/AAAAAAAAAOk/B0lbnmYNLak/s320/%2356.jpg" height="240" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/wp-content/uploads/2010/02/all.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://www.marinecsi.org/wp-content/uploads/2010/02/all.jpg" height="152" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;Great  white sharks are not resident to any given location, like say a clown  fish, where you know that if you go to that particular spot, you're  going to see that individual fish. The great white sharks that we see at  Guadalupe are a highly &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/wp-content/uploads/2010/05/Domeier-and-Nasby-Lucas-2013.pdf"&gt;migratory species&lt;/a&gt; that travel thousands of miles and typically return to the island each year. (every other year for adult females) &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So  here's the way I look at it. Say you live in a town or city, but I  don't have your address. If I just come into your town at random and  hang out, I may never run into you at all. With these sharks, I look at  the great wide ocean and know that I can find "Bite Face," "Jaques" or  "Bruce" and have been able to do so, consistently, for 13 years. Others,  like our friend on the left, &lt;a href="https://www.facebook.com/photo.php?fbid=10151663571454143&amp;amp;set=a.453534469142.246695.6891254142&amp;amp;type=1&amp;amp;theater"&gt;"Quetzalcoatl,"&lt;/a&gt;(OK I didn't name him) take a prolonged vacation of 8 years and return. "Where have you been, buddy?"&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The  fact that these world travelers (I mean, who doesn't want to vacation  in Hawaii) return to &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;, each season makes this Island a very  important place, not just for us shark divers, but for the species  itself. I'm happy to say that Mexico has declared the Island a  biosphere; roughly the equivalent of a national park in&amp;nbsp; the U.S. &amp;nbsp;I  want to applaud Mexico for taking that step in &lt;a href="http://www.conanp.gob.mx/english.php"&gt;protecting the Island&lt;/a&gt; and the great white sharks that visit there annually.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.tackletrader.com/Charter/Trips2002/PrivateBoat/082102Trip/LethalWeapon082202/GuadWeather.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://www.tackletrader.com/Charter/Trips2002/PrivateBoat/082102Trip/LethalWeapon082202/GuadWeather.jpg" height="200" width="200" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;The Island itself is a marvel of its own. There are many native species of plants that only exist on &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/tv"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt; and it is a nesting ground for many migratory birds like the Albatross.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Guadalupe  is over 4000 feet high at it's highest spot and creates its own weather  pattern. The island blocks the clouds and we usually have bright sunny  skies above us, even if it's cloudy all around us.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The clouds cascading over the mountains create an amazing backdrop for our &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.comm/"&gt;shark divers&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;and make for some memorable &lt;a href="http://www.oceanlight.com/stock-photo/white-cliffs-clouds-isla-guadalupe-photo-03848-897844.jpg"&gt;pictures&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You can join us on one of our expeditions and meet these shark yourself. We have a few openings left for this year and are already booking for 2016. For more information visit &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving/"&gt;http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving/ &lt;/a&gt;or call us at 619.887.4275. Email staff@sharkdiver.com&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let's go shark diving!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO&lt;br /&gt;Shark Diver&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.    As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation  initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks  around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these  dynamic and shifting worlds. title='Amazing!'/><author><name>Shark Diver</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/107965598445039841723</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='72'/><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-6460929051413817299</id><published>2015-04-26T10:16:00.000-07:00</published><updated>2015-04-26T10:16:29.234-07:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark conservation'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='cage diving'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='swimming with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='guadalupe island'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='new zealand'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><title type='text'>Shark "Documentary" causing problems in New Zealand</title><content type='html'>Shark diving in New Zealand has been in trouble for a while. The local Paua divers at Stewart Island are claiming that the shark diving activity is causing white sharks to change their behavior and are trying to get it banned.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-c4zd69DtLQM/VPX6VvjhQ1I/AAAAAAAABTQ/yQk49u9d4NI/s1600/shark%2Bsmile.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-c4zd69DtLQM/VPX6VvjhQ1I/AAAAAAAABTQ/yQk49u9d4NI/s1600/shark%2Bsmile.jpg" height="212" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.inquisitr.com/"&gt;The Inquisitor&lt;/a&gt; writes.&amp;nbsp;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Aggressive Great White Shark&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;! Behavioral Changes’ Spur Proposed Diving Ban In New Zealand                  &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;"&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;The behavior of great white sharks around  New Zealand’s Stewart Island has notably changed, according to local  Paua di&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;vers, prompting authorities to call for a ban on local shark  diving in light of the increasingly aggressive predators."&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;According to them&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;i&gt; "NZ First MP Clayton Mitchell noted the  frequency with which great whites were being observed by local  fishermen, asserting that the sharks are seen every day. He alleged that  this amounted to a change in the sharks’ behavior, raising fears among  the local Paua divers who make their living in the shark-infested  waters.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="copy-paste-block"&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;“They are very, very concerned about their safety. It’s not a matter  of if there’s an incident, but when and how often,” he noted. “Those  close encounters are happening more frequently, to the point where on a  daily basis when people are going out there and dropping a fishing line  into the ocean, sharks are coming up. That’s behavioral change.”&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Entire article &lt;a href="http://www.inquisitr.com/2029856/aggressive-great-white-shark-behavioral-changes-spur-proposed-diving-ban-in-new-zealand/"&gt;here:&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="copy-paste-block"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="copy-paste-block"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;I'm always amazed that fishermen blame shark diving, which uses some attractant (chum) and small hang-baits (tuna heads) are for "feeding" the sharks and thus making them associate boats with food. They themselves are feeding the sharks (unintentionally) with entire fish. A struggling fish, hooked on a line attracts predators and since they are on a line and not able to swim away, an easy meal for the sharks. Wouldn't it make sense that the fishermen themselves are &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;at least as much to blame for that association?&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="copy-paste-block"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-j42pLA3F04o/VT0W_06uTWI/AAAAAAAABYA/5tgaLkhzO_s/s1600/shark%2Bby%2Bcage.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-j42pLA3F04o/VT0W_06uTWI/AAAAAAAABYA/5tgaLkhzO_s/s1600/shark%2Bby%2Bcage.JPG" height="174" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="copy-paste-block"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="copy-paste-block"&gt;We know that when it comes to sharks, reason usually goes out the window and people argue mostly emotionally. As shark conservationists, we have to take that into consideration and need to be careful not to fuel their fear. And therein lies the problem. The need for some individuals, who claim to be conservationist, to make themselves look like superheros by doing all kinds of stupid stuff with those sharks and making it public, plays right into the hands of those who blame us for their behavior changes.&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="copy-paste-block"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="copy-paste-block"&gt;Today, the &lt;a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/"&gt;New Zealand Herald&lt;/a&gt; is reporting that a local group of Paua divers is using footage from a shark week "documentary" to claim that shark diving is to blame for sharks associating boats and humans with food.&amp;nbsp; They write: &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"Footage has emerged of the terrifying moment a 6m great white shark  lunged at a dinghy carrying an international film crew off Stewart  Island.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Two people were on the inflatable craft filming for documentary Lair of the Megashark, which screened on Discovery Channel last year, when they had the frightening encounter." &lt;a href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/nz/news/article.cfm?c_id=1&amp;amp;objectid=11438699"&gt;source&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;object width="320" height="266" class="BLOG_video_class" id="BLOG_video-4a0b3d248523567c" classid="clsid:D27CDB6E-AE6D-11cf-96B8-444553540000" codebase="http://download.macromedia.com/pub/shockwave/cabs/flash/swflash.cab#version=6,0,40,0"&gt;&lt;param name="movie" value="//www.youtube.com/get_player"&gt;&lt;param name="bgcolor" value="#FFFFFF"&gt;&lt;param name="allowfullscreen" value="true"&gt;&lt;param name="flashvars" value="flvurl=https://redirector.googlevideo.com/videoplayback?requiressl%3Dyes%26id%3D4a0b3d248523567c%26itag%3D5%26source%3Dblogger%26app%3Dblogger%26cmo%3Dsecure_transport%253Dyes%26cmo%3Dsensitive_content%253Dyes%26ip%3D0.0.0.0%26ipbits%3D0%26expire%3D1495466272%26sparams%3Drequiressl,id,itag,source,ip,ipbits,expire%26signature%3D2782BC1C13D0A556E15A8EE18110DEFFC46653B4.D23D989FE3ECB0D7BE2F339EB74040ED6A2F777%26key%3Dck2&amp;amp;iurl=http://video.google.com/ThumbnailServer2?app%3Dblogger%26contentid%3D4a0b3d248523567c%26offsetms%3D5000%26itag%3Dw160%26sigh%3Du5inIGx2w-mudv-Rx1bEoe4j9zo&amp;amp;autoplay=0&amp;amp;ps=blogger"&gt;&lt;embed src="//www.youtube.com/get_player" type="application/x-shockwave-flash" width="320" height="266" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" flashvars="flvurl=https://redirector.googlevideo.com/videoplayback?requiressl%3Dyes%26id%3D4a0b3d248523567c%26itag%3D5%26source%3Dblogger%26app%3Dblogger%26cmo%3Dsecure_transport%253Dyes%26cmo%3Dsensitive_content%253Dyes%26ip%3D0.0.0.0%26ipbits%3D0%26expire%3D1495466272%26sparams%3Drequiressl,id,itag,source,ip,ipbits,expire%26signature%3D2782BC1C13D0A556E15A8EE18110DEFFC46653B4.D23D989FE3ECB0D7BE2F339EB74040ED6A2F777%26key%3Dck2&amp;iurl=http://video.google.com/ThumbnailServer2?app%3Dblogger%26contentid%3D4a0b3d248523567c%26offsetms%3D5000%26itag%3Dw160%26sigh%3Du5inIGx2w-mudv-Rx1bEoe4j9zo&amp;autoplay=0&amp;ps=blogger" allowFullScreen="true" /&gt;&lt;/object&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span id="goog_258196530"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span id="goog_258196531"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In this video that was put &lt;a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=tHih0KrwcgE"&gt;online&lt;/a&gt;, you can see the filmmakers put a hang-bait right by the boat to attract the shark. When the shark goes after it, they make it seem like it was going after the boat itself.&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt; Stuff like that doesn't help to spread the message that great white sharks are not mindless killers.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;This "documentary" is of course by none other than renowned "shark porn" producers &lt;a href="http://www.ew.com/article/2014/08/12/shark-week-lair-mega-shark"&gt;ABC4 and Jeff Kurr.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Jeff Kurr is making statements like this:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: magenta;"&gt; I’ve been wondering about why the sharks in New Zealand are so much more aggressive.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;span style="color: magenta;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt; and &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: magenta;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;I can’t think of many things more eerie than descending into this inky  blackness and being surrounded by three, four, six, eight massive great  white sharks. That’s pretty scary stuff.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;a href="http://www.ew.com/article/2014/08/12/shark-week-lair-mega-shark"&gt;source&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So he's making a statement of fact, white sharks in New Zealand are more aggressive than in other places. What an "expert"! (sharkasm intended) Him saying that it's pretty scary stuff to be surrounded by &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt; isn't exactly easing the fears of those Paua divers. Of course the titles of their "documentaries" "Lair of the megashark" and "Fins of Fury" doesn't help either.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;There are many studies that dispute that shark diving will cause the &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt; to attack boats, but like anything having to do with &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt;, hysteria and opinions seem to trump facts. When these "experts" and self proclaimed "shark whisperers" fuel that hysteria just to get ratings for their shows, or further their superhero image, they hurt the cause severely.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;The bottom line is this, if we as an industry don't speak out against these kinds of shows and actively participate by allowing them to film this stuff off our vessels, we hurt not only conservation, but our own businesses. The operators in New Zealand have been finding that out the hard way.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;I have stated this before. You may have mixed feelings about &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark diving&lt;/a&gt;, but one thing is clear. At &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/tv"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt; we have been chasing off poachers in the past. If for some reason the cage diving there gets shut down, there will be nobody looking out for the sharks and the poachers will have free reign.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-Q6Z-9vDLtik/VCwogtAmXyI/AAAAAAAABHw/6RjNx65bwIE/s1600/August%2B9-88.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-Q6Z-9vDLtik/VCwogtAmXyI/AAAAAAAABHw/6RjNx65bwIE/s1600/August%2B9-88.JPG" height="179" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;So let's go shark diving! But let's do it legally, responsibly, safely and in a way that portrays the sharks as what they really are, awesome predators, to be respected but not to be feared!&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Cheers,&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Martin Graf&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&amp;nbsp;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. witness reports large great white</title><content type='html'>&lt;b&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.foxnews.com/"&gt;FOX news&lt;/a&gt; has this headline today &lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;"&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;Surfer critically injured by shark off southern Australia; witness reports large great white"&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;The following is what&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;they report:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div itemprop="articleBody"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span class="dateline"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.foxnews.com/world/2015/04/25/surfer-critically-injured-by-shark-off-southern-australia-witness-reports-large/"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span class="dateline"&gt;"ADELAIDE, Australia – &amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;A surfer is in critical condition after a shark attacked him in southern Australia.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.foxnews.com/world/2015/04/25/surfer-critically-injured-by-shark-off-southern-australia-witness-reports-large/"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;              &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.foxnews.com/world/2015/04/25/surfer-critically-injured-by-shark-off-southern-australia-witness-reports-large/"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Police  said in a statement that the 26-year-old man suffered "serious leg  injuries" when he was attacked Saturday about 40 kilometers (25 miles)  south of Port Lincoln in South Australia state.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.foxnews.com/world/2015/04/25/surfer-critically-injured-by-shark-off-southern-australia-witness-reports-large/"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;              &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.foxnews.com/world/2015/04/25/surfer-critically-injured-by-shark-off-southern-australia-witness-reports-large/"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;He  was flown by helicopter in critical condition from a Port Lincoln  hospital to the main hospital in the state capital, Adelaide.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.foxnews.com/world/2015/04/25/surfer-critically-injured-by-shark-off-southern-australia-witness-reports-large/"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;              &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.foxnews.com/world/2015/04/25/surfer-critically-injured-by-shark-off-southern-australia-witness-reports-large/"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Adelaide's  The Advertiser newspaper reported a witness's description of a 6-meter  (20-foot) great white shark biting off the surfer's leg, which had an  ankle strap attached to his surfboard.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.foxnews.com/world/2015/04/25/surfer-critically-injured-by-shark-off-southern-australia-witness-reports-large/"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;              &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.foxnews.com/world/2015/04/25/surfer-critically-injured-by-shark-off-southern-australia-witness-reports-large/"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Sharks are common off Australia's beaches, but fatal attacks are rare. The country has averaged fewer than two deadly attacks per year in recent decades."&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have to say, that I'm usually not a big fan of how the media reports any shark related incident. Take the &lt;a href="http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/04/giant-shark-scare-in-uk.html"&gt;"Jaws Attack"&lt;/a&gt;&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;headline in the UK we talked about yesterday and you can see how sensationalistic the media tends to cover anything &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt; related.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-Mw5BoT_RGOg/UiEE9Oj_EgI/AAAAAAAAAOo/SgKe0QWz41I/s1600/%2356.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-Mw5BoT_RGOg/UiEE9Oj_EgI/AAAAAAAAAOo/SgKe0QWz41I/s1600/%2356.jpg" height="240" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;I like not being described as a mindless killer!&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Big kudos to &lt;a href="http://www.foxnews.com/"&gt;FOX news&lt;/a&gt; for reporting an actual incident, where a surfer got seriously hurt by a shark and cover it without any sensationalism.&amp;nbsp; Maybe the 20 foot size is a bit exaggerated, but people tend to perceive sharks a larger than they actually are. They even pointed out the fact that &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks &lt;/a&gt;are common off Australia's beaches and attacks are rare.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO Shark Diver &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. writes &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;"Jaws attack: Terror after GIANT SHARKS spotted circling the coast of England"&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Wow, someone got attacked by a &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;giant shark&lt;/a&gt;! Did they survive? What kind of a shark was it?&lt;br /&gt;The article states: "&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;HOLIDAYMAKERS have been placed on alert as huge sharks hit British shores thanks to the recent hot weather.&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Still, no mention of what happened. So what the heck is going on?&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;object classid="clsid:D27CDB6E-AE6D-11cf-96B8-444553540000" codebase="http://download.macromedia.com/pub/shockwave/cabs/flash/swflash.cab#version=9,0,47,0" height="270" id="flashObj" width="480"&gt;&lt;param name="movie" value="http://c.brightcove.com/services/viewer/federated_f9?isVid=1&amp;isUI=1" /&gt;&lt;param name="bgcolor" value="#FFFFFF" /&gt;&lt;param name="flashVars" value="videoId=4182635758001&amp;playerID=2538956444001&amp;playerKey=AQ~~,AAACT2hWexE~,QV-ElXQT89XEkLQHlpWPz_5DAA2-uG70&amp;domain=embed&amp;dynamicStreaming=true" /&gt;&lt;param name="base" value="http://admin.brightcove.com" /&gt;&lt;param name="seamlesstabbing" value="false" /&gt;&lt;param name="allowFullScreen" value="true" /&gt;&lt;param name="swLiveConnect" value="true" /&gt;&lt;param name="allowScriptAccess" value="always" /&gt;&lt;embed src="http://c.brightcove.com/services/viewer/federated_f9?isVid=1&amp;isUI=1" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" flashVars="videoId=4182635758001&amp;playerID=2538956444001&amp;playerKey=AQ~~,AAACT2hWexE~,QV-ElXQT89XEkLQHlpWPz_5DAA2-uG70&amp;domain=embed&amp;dynamicStreaming=true" base="http://admin.brightcove.com" name="flashObj" width="480" height="270" seamlesstabbing="false" type="application/x-shockwave-flash" allowFullScreen="true" allowScriptAccess="always" swLiveConnect="true" pluginspage="http://www.macromedia.com/shockwave/download/index.cgi?P1_Prod_Version=ShockwaveFlash"&gt;&lt;/embed&gt;&lt;/object&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;OK, we are getting somewhere. Here is what happened: &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"The basking sharks, which can grow up to 26ft long, have been spotted off beaches in many of the country's holiday hotspots.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;As if that wasn't terrifying enough – thousands of jellyfish have also been spotted in the waves."&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;The caption for the picture below read: &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;"&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span class="caption"&gt;HORROR: The terrifying sharks – which can grow up  to 26ft – have started circling shallow water around the UK [AK Wildlife  Cruises]"&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://images.dailystar-uk.co.uk/dynamic/1/photos/401000/620x/5533e9465921f_shark1.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://images.dailystar-uk.co.uk/dynamic/1/photos/401000/620x/5533e9465921f_shark1.jpg" height="266" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://images.dailystar-uk.co.uk/dynamic/1/photos/401000/620x/5533e9465921f_shark1.jpg"&gt;&lt;span class="caption"&gt;&lt;i&gt;source&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Wait, did I miss something? Where is the attack? What is terrifying about a basking shark?&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;The article goes on to say:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt; "Ross Wheeler of AK Wildlife Cruises in Falmouth, Cornwall, captured  incredible footage of the first sighting of a shark in UK waters."We  had two basking sharks – our first for the season – thousands of barrel  jellyfish, 11 common dolphin and five harbour porpoise" he said."&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Ah, I see. They are describing some people going on a wildlife cruise and encountering a completely harmless basking shark. The "reporter" mistakenly wrote the wrong headline. He really meant to say: "Tourists are excited about encountering gentle giant" or "Lucky tourists encounter gentle giant and friendly dolphins off the UK coast". Easy mistake to make (sharkasm) intended.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Later on the article correctly mentions: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"But the sighting isn't likely to mean a repeat of horrific scenes  from 1975 thriller Jaws - the basking sharks are harmless but have been  lured to the Cornish coastline earlier than normal.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;They swim around with their gaping jaws open to swallow tiny plankton, their main food source."&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;So the reporter actually knew that there was no attack and the sharks are harmless plankton eaters, which of course didn't stop him from making up a completely fictitious and sensationalistic headline. It's not like the sharks don't have it hard enough already, with overfishing and being killed for their fins. I really wish the media would stop making it worse by portraying even the most harmless sharks as terrifying monsters.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Cheers,&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Martin Graf&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;CEO Shark Diver&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Check out the trailer below.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;iframe allowfullscreen="" class="YOUTUBE-iframe-video" data-thumbnail-src="https://i.ytimg.com/vi/21hGAKv_0Bs/0.jpg" frameborder="0" height="366" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/21hGAKv_0Bs?feature=player_embedded" width="420"&gt;&lt;/iframe&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div deployment="76671961nn7sah" id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.yekra.com/revolution"&gt;&amp;nbsp;Revolution &lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Revolution is a feature documentary about opening your eyes, changing the world and fighting for something. A true life adventure following director Rob Stewart in the follow up to his hit Sharkwater, Revolution is an epic adventure into the evolution of life on earth and the revolution to save us.&lt;br /&gt;Discovering that there’s more in jeopardy than sharks, Stewart uncovers a grave secret threatening our own survival as a species, and embarks on a life-threatening adventure through 4 years and 15 countries into the greatest battle ever waged.&lt;br /&gt;Bringing you some of the most incredible wildlife spectacles ever recorded, audiences are brought face to face with sharks and cuddly lemurs, into the microscopic world of the pygmy seahorse, and on the hunt with the deadly flamboyant cuttlefish. From the coral reefs in Papua New Guinea to the rain forests in Madagascar, Stewart reveals that our fate is tied to even the smallest of creatures.&lt;br /&gt;Through it all, Stewart’s journey reveals a massive opportunity, as activists and individuals all over the world are winning the battle to save the ecosystems we depend on for survival. Presenting the most important information on human survival and inspiring people all over the world to fight for life, Revolution is essential viewing for everyone. Startling, beautiful, and provocative, Revolution inspires audiences across the globe to join the biggest movement in history that’s rising to the challenge of saving our world.&lt;br /&gt;Revolution premiered at the Toronto International Film Festival and has already gone on to win ten awards, including the Audience Award for Best Documentary at the Atlantic Film Festival, Most Popular Environmental Film Award at the Vancouver International Film Festival, the Audience Award at the Victoria Film Festival and the Social Justice Award at the Santa Barbara International Film Festival.&lt;/div&gt;&lt;script src="https://www.yekra.com/javascripts/embed.js"&gt; &lt;/script&gt; &lt;br /&gt;&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO Shark Diver&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.
