scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark diver'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark conservation'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='BAD'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='earth day'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Beqa Adventure Divers'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='mangroves for fiji'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='projecs abroad'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='fiji'/><title type='text'>Conservation done right. BAD is good!</title><content type='html'>&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;Today, on Earth Day, as we are getting ready for our Fiji trip, to dive with bull sharks at the Beqa &lt;a href="http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2014/10/shark-conservation-at-its-best.html"&gt;Shark Reef Marine Reserve&lt;/a&gt;, we get some news about why we love that place so much. It's not just because they have some of the &lt;a href="http://www.fijisharkdive.com/"&gt;best shark diving&lt;/a&gt; in the world.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;5 years ago, &lt;a href="https://www.blogger.com/profile/06787762757245289307"&gt;DaShark&lt;/a&gt; started &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/2010/09/mangroves-for-fiji.html"&gt;"Mangroves for Fiji"&lt;/a&gt; in order for &lt;a href="http://www.fijisharkdive.com/"&gt;Beqa Adventure Divers &lt;/a&gt;"BAD"  (It really means "Bad Ass Divers") and other Fiji businesses to become carbon neutral.&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Whether it is their dive  operation  or their commitment to conservation, everything they do is a cut above.  No wonder they describe themselves as a conservation project  masquerading as a dive shop. You may remember, that it was also they who  were instrumental in creating the first &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/2014/10/shark-reef-marine-reserve-breaking-news.html"&gt;marine national park&lt;/a&gt; in Fiji. &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-exs2XoWTLbE/VTeBnyGujCI/AAAAAAAAOF8/JVSqffBXPh4/s1600/Picture1.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-exs2XoWTLbE/VTeBnyGujCI/AAAAAAAAOF8/JVSqffBXPh4/s1600/Picture1.jpg" height="231" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://mangrovesforfiji.com/"&gt;Mangroves for Fiji&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp; just released their website, &lt;a href="http://mangrovesforfiji.com/"&gt;"Mangroves for Fiji"&lt;/a&gt; where businesses can sign up to become carbon neutral. You can check out and like their &lt;a href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Mangroves-for-Fiji/412911885553899?sk=timeline"&gt;Facebook page&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://mangrovesforfiji.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/Galoa-Village-086.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://mangrovesforfiji.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/Galoa-Village-086.jpg" height="212" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.projects-abroad.net/"&gt;Projects Abroad&lt;/a&gt;, who is planting those mangroves on "BAD's" behalf has some exciting volunteer opportunities for you to help with their shark conservation program. Check &lt;a href="http://www.projects-abroad.co.uk/volunteer-destinations/fiji/conservation-and-environment/shark-conservation/"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt; for details. I can tell you from personal experience, volunteering with them is a blast. You couldn't possibly have more fun, doing something for the environment, than working with &lt;a href="http://www.projects-abroad.co.uk/volunteer-destinations/fiji/conservation-and-environment/shark-conservation/"&gt;Projects Abroad in Fiji&lt;/a&gt;. I had a blast, trying to tag some bull shark with them last year.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-jlG8YSanWKE/U35NLo1fPsI/AAAAAAAAA5M/GK_PtPMYMk0/s1600/XD5V1869-293.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-jlG8YSanWKE/U35NLo1fPsI/AAAAAAAAA5M/GK_PtPMYMk0/s1600/XD5V1869-293.JPG" height="213" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; is proud to partner with &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdive.com/"&gt;"BAD"&lt;/a&gt; for our bull &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/bull-shark-diving-fiji/"&gt;shark expedition in May&lt;/a&gt;. You can also book your shark dive with "BAD" for anytime of the year through us. Call us at 855.987.4275 or email staff@sharkdiver.com for more info.&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;I can't wait to travel to Fiji next month and see the progress they have made first hand. &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Have a great Earth Day!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO Shark Diver&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="yekra-player" name="YekraPlayer" rel="406" sizing="auto"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;script src="https://www.yekra.com/javascripts/embed.js"&gt; &lt;/script&gt; &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. You can reach us directly at staff@sharkdiver.com.</content><link rel='replies' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/feeds/1033389635706996783/comments/default' title='Post Comments'/><link rel='replies' type='text/html' href='https://www.blogger.com/comment.g?blogID=370711998877298323&amp;postID=1033389635706996783' title='0 Comments'/><link rel='edit' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/1033389635706996783'/><link rel='self' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/1033389635706996783'/><link rel='alternate' type='text/html' href='http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/04/conservation-done-right-bad-is-good.html' title='Conservation done right. BAD is good!'/><author><name>Shark Diver</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/107965598445039841723</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='32' height='32' src='//lh5.googleusercontent.com/-acNbaifFSTQ/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAB_A/inqVjDI-1J8/s32-c/photo.jpg'/></author><media:thumbnail xmlns:media='http://search.yahoo.com/mrss/' url='http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-exs2XoWTLbE/VTeBnyGujCI/AAAAAAAAOF8/JVSqffBXPh4/s72-c/Picture1.jpg' height='72' width='72'/><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-3657237211721818588</id><published>2015-04-17T08:40:00.000-07:00</published><updated>2015-04-17T08:40:09.578-07:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark diver'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark conservation'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Ian Campbell. wwf'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='diving with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><title type='text'>How every diver can help with shark conservation.</title><content type='html'>I have to share &lt;a href="https://www.blogger.com/profile/06787762757245289307"&gt;DaSharks &lt;/a&gt;latest blog. It is actually a &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/2015/04/shark-rat-guest-post-by-ian-campbell.html"&gt;guest blog&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;by Ian Campbell&lt;/a&gt; that talks about protecting &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt; and how you can help. &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: left; margin-right: 1em; text-align: left;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-yFhF7YaPsfM/VTC9437h6AI/AAAAAAAAODk/d-FZpqaN9Qk/s1600/Group%2Bpicture.jpg" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="205" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-yFhF7YaPsfM/VTC9437h6AI/AAAAAAAAODk/d-FZpqaN9Qk/s400/Group%2Bpicture.jpg" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: xx-small;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: #666666;"&gt;Shark research, management &amp;amp; conservation intelligentsia meeting in Townsville, see below&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Introduction by DaSharks:&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Are you intrigued? :)&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Here goes.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Ian Campbell is currently working for WWF’s Global Shark and Ray  Initiative running the sustainable management component. He is also a  Shark diver and a member of the &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/2014/11/wwf-shark-reef-marine-reserve.html"&gt;SRMR management team&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;From NGOs to the public and private sector, Ian has over 20 years’  experience in fisheries policy, ecology and fishery management working  extensively within both the UK and internationally. Previous employment  has included overseeing the reform of the EU’s Common Fisheries Policy  for the Pew Charitable Trusts, fisheries observer on blue-fin tuna  vessels, inshore fisheries management and as a commercial diver in the  offshore sector.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Ian holds a Bachelor’s degree in Applied Marine Biology from  Heriot-Watt University and a Master degree in Environmental Science from  the University of Strathclyde.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;This is an important initiative.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Having just returned from a meeting with major stakeholders, see at  top, I've asked him whether he wouldn't mind submitting a guest post  presenting it to the wider public.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Here is Ian's post.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;b&gt;Shark divers – An underused resource?&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Everyone who is even remotely interested in sharks (and rays, don’t forget these &lt;a href="https://www.pinterest.com/dulvy/charismatic-pancakes-of-wonder/"&gt;charismatic shark pancakes of wonder&lt;/a&gt;) is abundantly aware of the pressures they are facing.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Fishing pressure, habitat loss, unsustainable consumption, or even fanciful claims of being “&lt;a href="http://www.rsmas.miami.edu/assets/BioScience-2014-Gallagher-biosci-biu071.pdf"&gt;evolved for extinction&lt;/a&gt;” everywhere you look they are under the cosh. The pressure that sharks are under have probably best been summed up by the &lt;a href="http://cmsdata.iucn.org/downloads/fact_sheets.pdf"&gt;2014 paper&lt;/a&gt; (and &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/2014/01/iucn-shark-paper.html"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt; - notice the part about research and data collection?)  led by the IUCN Shark Specialist Group which concludes that almost a  quarter of all sharks and rays (over 1,000 species assessed) are faced  with the very real threat of extinction. Remember, this is not the  claims of an environmental NGO, but an independent assessment of the  current state of shark and ray populations by 128 experts from 35  different countries. Here’s a simple chart highlighting the different  levels of threat.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-thFQbi5og0k/VTC51IzMAnI/AAAAAAAAODY/CaMPnJCLZbQ/s1600/sharks%2Band%2Brays.png" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="268" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-thFQbi5og0k/VTC51IzMAnI/AAAAAAAAODY/CaMPnJCLZbQ/s1600/sharks%2Band%2Brays.png" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;As you can see, despite what you may hear from some campaigns, not all  sharks are threatened, and some are in worse shape than others, but, for  WWF, one of the biggest areas of concern is the shaded grey area on the  left side of that chart. From all the 1,042 species assessed, 487 are  “data deficient”.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Basically, virtually nothing is known about almost &lt;b&gt;half&lt;/b&gt; of all sharks and rays.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Effective management and designing plans to reduce mortality is  virtually impossible when faced with this lack of basic understanding.  Imagine trying to balance your budget without knowing how much money you  have in your account to start with, or the amount of interest you are  receiving or paying out.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;There are a number of conservation initiatives out there which lay  claims to conserving sharks, from finning bans to fin trade bans  (there’s a difference), from sanctuaries to species protections and from  policies to plans. Some of these are more useful than others, but if  any of them are to be truly effectual then one thing is key to them all:  &lt;b&gt;DATA!&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Without a basic understanding of shark and ray populations both around  the coast and in offshore waters, then making decisions for the  long-term survival of these species is little more than a best guess.  Yet there are a multitude of areas rich in information, but not  necessarily being channeled in the right direction.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Divers, fishermen, market traders, even shark and ray researchers  produce data every day, yet it is surprising how little of it actually  makes its way to ministerial departments or independent bodies to assist  with informed decisions for conservation. WWF are seeking to bridge  this gap. We are developing a project in collaboration with some of the  world’s leading shark researchers to create standard methodologies to  maximize the benefits from untapped resources. &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;In 1999, the Food and Agriculture Organisation produced guidelines for  countries to undertake a step-by-step process to developing long-term,  sustainable shark management plans (known as National Plans of Action,  NPOA).&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;This process seems relatively simple. Firstly, collect data on sharks  and rays in the form of a Shark Assessment Report. Then use this data to  develop your NPOA. While this does sound simple, and has been done in  places like Australia, the EU and NZ (to varying degrees of vigour), the  Pacific Islands have had to get by using the limited resources at their  disposal. There are some NPOAs currently in existence in the region,  such as the Cook Islands and Samoa. Other countries have draft versions  waiting government endorsement, such Fiji and Tonga, while some  countries such as Palau want to declare shark sanctuaries. These efforts  for conservation &amp;amp; long-term planning are great, although all of  these measures have one oversight in common. They are built on a lack of  data. None of the countries have produced Shark Assessment Reports, so  cannot fully know the issues within their territorial waters. This is  not the fault of the Pacific Islands, gathering data can be time  consuming for departments with limited resources, and the analysis  requires specific technical expertise. Organizations such as the &lt;a href="https://www.ffa.int/"&gt;FFA&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="http://www.spc.int/"&gt;SPC&lt;/a&gt; are providing a great service, although their remit extends way beyond just looking at sharks.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;So here is where WWF are stepping in.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;As mentioned, we are collaborating with shark expertise far and wide to  develop our shark ‘Rapid Assessment Tool-kit’ (or shark RAT). The main  function of this is to design ways to collect and analyze data on  coastal and pelagic sharks that can then be used to produce a Shark  Assessment Report. The very basic baseline data in this report can in  turn used by governments to develop conservation strategies that are  then based on some sort of understanding.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Where is this data going to come from?&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Well, there are a lot of sources we will be exploring from genetic and  socioeconomic surveys at landing sites to extensive underwater video  surveys, but one untapped goldmine is the information collected by  divers. In Fiji, there is the &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/search/label/The%20Great%20Fiji%20Shark%20Count"&gt;Great Fiji Shark Count&lt;/a&gt; which is starting to produce comparable info. At present, this isn’t  incorporated into management plans, so it’s high time it is. &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;There are also other things dedicated shark divers can be doing.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Ever been on a surface interval that seems to go on for ages? Sat at the  bar for the post-dive drinks to talk about what you saw? How about  these hours are spent helping screen underwater video footage that shows  what happens at your dive site when no-one is in the water? Pretty much  every diver would be able to recognise whether a shark or ray was in  shot, and a huge number would even be able to say what species it was.  Collecting and screening this type of data would take a massive burden  off an already overstretched ministry or fisheries/shark specialist.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Obviously, we are well aware of the multitude of challenges that lay  ahead for the project to be fully successful, and some methodologies  that may look good on the page may fail spectacularly when introduced to  the real world. But we have to try. Improved management for sharks and  rays is the only thing that is going to directly reduce mortality. Not  shark fin soup campaigns, or putting all your eggs into “ending finning”  and certainly not cavorting in swimwear near sharks.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Last week WWF held a 3 day workshop where 12 of the best minds in their  respective fields (I’m not including myself, I just took notes and  provided the tea and coffee) provided input and direction.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;As well as academic researchers from the fields of genetics, citizen science and eco-tourism, we had input from FFA, SPC and &lt;a href="http://www.sprep.org/"&gt;SPREP&lt;/a&gt;.  Everyone we have spoken to has been enthusiastic and willing to support  us. The people in attendance will now provide advice and  recommendations to the project. &lt;a href="https://www.google.com/search?q=Prof+Colin+Simpfendorfer&amp;amp;ie=utf-8&amp;amp;oe=utf-8"&gt;Professor Colin Simpfendorfer&lt;/a&gt;,  the co-chair of the IUCN Shark Specialist Group also gave us a name,  although how serious he was is up for debate. WWF now convenes the  Pacific Rapid Assessment Tool-kit Scientific Advisory Committee, or  PRAT-SAC. Maybe the first thing we need to work on is the name? &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;The project is embryonic and there is a lot of hard work ahead, but with  a little direction, continued enthusiasm and, more importantly,  collaboration, then slowly we’ll &lt;a href="http://wwf.panda.org/what_we_do/endangered_species/sharks/"&gt;restore the balance&lt;/a&gt; for sharks and rays&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;DaShark: Here's to that - thanks buddy, appreciate!&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Thanks indeed! I hope all of you will join in this effort to conserve our &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiving.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt; populations. And here you were, thinking you're just having fun, when you're &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving/"&gt;diving with sharks&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let's go &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving/"&gt;shark diving&lt;/a&gt;!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO Shark Diver&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark tagging'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='swimming with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark conservations'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark fishing'/><title type='text'>Working with Fishermen to Save Sharks</title><content type='html'>The shark conservation and fishing communities are often at odds over protecting our sharks. &lt;a href="http://www.guyharveymagazine.com/"&gt;Guy Harvey&lt;/a&gt; is making an effort to bring these two groups together. During the current Cayman Islands International Fishing Tournament, he is teaming up with the participants to help tag oceanic white tip &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://d2ouvy59p0dg6k.cloudfront.net/img/original/hi_257599.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://d2ouvy59p0dg6k.cloudfront.net/img/original/hi_257599.jpg" height="266" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://d2ouvy59p0dg6k.cloudfront.net/img/original/hi_257599.jpg"&gt;source&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.cayman27.com.ky/2015/04/15/shark-tagging-programme-enlists-fishermen"&gt;Cayman 27&lt;/a&gt; writes: &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"Dozens of fishermen are getting in on the conservation act by helping to  tag sharks. Conservationist Dr. Guy Harvey is teaming up with  participants of the Cayman Islands International Fishing Tournament,  embarking on one of the largest shark tagging and research projects ever  undertaken in the Caribbean.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Dr. Harvey’s team will learn more about the oceanic white tip shark.  “They are very valuable to the eco-system and to science,” he says.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;By aligning with local fishing tournaments in 2013, as well as this  year he believes fishermen are becoming more aware of the shark’s worth.  “We used the fishing fleet to catch sharks for us and we pay them to  hold the sharks until the chase boat [gets] there there to take the  sharks from them because they’re giving up time for us,” explained Mr.  Harvey."&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;I know, a lot of conservationists don't like fishing tournaments and even oppose actions like these by Guy Harvey. They think this is glorifying the killing of &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt; and argue that there is post release mortality. I have to admit,&amp;nbsp; I'm not a big fan of catch and release &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt; fishing myself, but think about it this way. What is better? Going to a shark fishing tournament and protesting, maybe even hurling some insults at the fishermen, questioning their morals and character, like many people like to do, or do what Guy Harvey is doing?&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;object width="440" height="366" class="BLOG_video_class" id="BLOG_video-21bc28d52f620383" classid="clsid:D27CDB6E-AE6D-11cf-96B8-444553540000" codebase="http://download.macromedia.com/pub/shockwave/cabs/flash/swflash.cab#version=6,0,40,0"&gt;&lt;param name="movie" value="//www.youtube.com/get_player"&gt;&lt;param name="bgcolor" value="#FFFFFF"&gt;&lt;param name="allowfullscreen" value="true"&gt;&lt;param name="flashvars" value="flvurl=https://redirector.googlevideo.com/videoplayback?requiressl%3Dyes%26id%3D21bc28d52f620383%26itag%3D5%26source%3Dblogger%26app%3Dblogger%26cmo%3Dsecure_transport%253Dyes%26cmo%3Dsensitive_content%253Dyes%26ip%3D0.0.0.0%26ipbits%3D0%26expire%3D1495466272%26sparams%3Drequiressl,id,itag,source,ip,ipbits,expire%26signature%3DB5061EC9857747F966B6E24983475FCE93FEFB10.9BF66E6CAB39FBDD4A562DD21D4F52887B10B1DE%26key%3Dck2&amp;amp;iurl=http://video.google.com/ThumbnailServer2?app%3Dblogger%26contentid%3D21bc28d52f620383%26offsetms%3D5000%26itag%3Dw160%26sigh%3DYpDNODvyVD5Ecb4kYmglve_GWj8&amp;amp;autoplay=0&amp;amp;ps=blogger"&gt;&lt;embed flashvars="flvurl=https://redirector.googlevideo.com/videoplayback?requiressl%3Dyes%26id%3D21bc28d52f620383%26itag%3D5%26source%3Dblogger%26app%3Dblogger%26cmo%3Dsecure_transport%253Dyes%26cmo%3Dsensitive_content%253Dyes%26ip%3D0.0.0.0%26ipbits%3D0%26expire%3D1495466272%26sparams%3Drequiressl,id,itag,source,ip,ipbits,expire%26signature%3DB5061EC9857747F966B6E24983475FCE93FEFB10.9BF66E6CAB39FBDD4A562DD21D4F52887B10B1DE%26key%3Dck2&amp;iurl=http://video.google.com/ThumbnailServer2?app%3Dblogger%26contentid%3D21bc28d52f620383%26offsetms%3D5000%26itag%3Dw160%26sigh%3DYpDNODvyVD5Ecb4kYmglve_GWj8&amp;autoplay=0&amp;ps=blogger" allowFullScreen="true" /&gt;&lt;/object&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Just like the &lt;a href="http://sharkfriendlymarinas.org/"&gt;Shark Free Marina&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;initiative that was created by &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;, Harvey is working together with the fishermen in these tournaments. He raises their awareness of the conservation concerns and gets them interested and involved in protecting the &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt;.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;"Cayman 27's" &lt;a href="http://www.cayman27.com.ky/2015/04/15/shark-tagging-programme-enlists-fishermen"&gt;article&lt;/a&gt; states:&amp;nbsp; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;“For  every shark that you get and call in; that we successfully tag and  release [fishermen] will receive CI$500 in cash,” said CIB Marketing  Manager, Matthew Leslie.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;And the partnership is working says Dr. Harvey, by the fishermen  getting to see the animals in their offshore habitat, he says anglers  are practicing preservation.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;We always have to ask ourselves this question. Do we care more about the principle that we should not catch or kill any sharks, or do we want to save sharks. By protesting and vilifying the fishermen, we will not save one shark! By working with them, promoting catch and release, (even with all the problems associated with that), getting them to help with tagging and making em aware, we actually save sharks. &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Every journey starts with a first step. We are never going to accomplish our goal of saving the sharks, the oceans, if we are not willing to work together.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO Shark Diver&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark media'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark sightings'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><title type='text'>Shark sighting in Portugal</title><content type='html'>Congratulations to the &lt;a href="http://www.algarvedailynews.com/"&gt;algarvedailynews&lt;/a&gt;!&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;You managed to cover a shark sighting near shore without sensationalism, with a simple "&lt;a href="http://www.algarvedailynews.com/news/5304-mystery-shark-spotted-near-tavira"&gt;Mystery shark spotted near Tavira&lt;/a&gt;" headline.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In the article you go on to explaine exactly what happened.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;As the build up to the swimming season  starts with beaches being prepared and concession soon to open, a  reminder that 'we are not alone' when bathing was evident in the waters  near Tavira.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;A shark at least two metres long was spotted by fishermen on the jetty close to the beaches at the entrance of the river Gilão.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://cdn.cmjornal.xl.pt/2015-04/img_757x426$2015_04_09_13_01_12_445736.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://cdn.cmjornal.xl.pt/2015-04/img_757x426$2015_04_09_13_01_12_445736.jpg" height="225" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;Photo Michael Correia - Correio da Manhã&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;  &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;The shark clearly was in distress and was disorientated, swimming around in the shallow waters.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;After an hour the shark headed back out  to sea with its identity a mystery as, despite being observed by many  fishermen, nobody could identify the species.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;The Tavira shark was not a Hammerhead, a  species which can come close to the shore but normally feeds at least a  mile out mainly on sardines, tuna and mackerel and only when the water  is warmer at 20 degrees or more.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;In 2013 a three metre shark was spotted  close in to the shore near the fortress at Sagres, again the species  could not be acertained. &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Along Portugal’s coast there are dozens  of shark species, the majority of which stay offshore and deep down,  venturing closer to the surface only when hunting for fish or looking  for a mate.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;There is an abundance of sharks in  Portuguese waters, a sign of a healthy marine environment, but no  recorded incident of anyone being attacked as sharks prefer eating fish  of which there are plentiful supplies.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Kudos for reporting a &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt; sighting without sensationalism and resorting to the use of monster, beast or killer. You informed your readers, without scaring them. Your action shows that covering a shark sighting can be done in an informative manner and no scary headlines. I hope that other media outlets will take note.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Cheers,&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Martin Graf&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;CEO Shark Diver&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. You can reach us directly at staff@sharkdiver.com.</content><link rel='replies' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/feeds/5092360259820398871/comments/default' title='Post Comments'/><link rel='replies' type='text/html' href='https://www.blogger.com/comment.g?blogID=370711998877298323&amp;postID=5092360259820398871' title='0 Comments'/><link rel='edit' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/5092360259820398871'/><link rel='self' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/5092360259820398871'/><link rel='alternate' type='text/html' href='http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/04/shark-sighting-in-portugal.html' title='Shark sighting in Portugal'/><author><name>Shark Diver</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/107965598445039841723</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='32' height='32' src='//lh5.googleusercontent.com/-acNbaifFSTQ/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAB_A/inqVjDI-1J8/s32-c/photo.jpg'/></author><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-5176217903761629640</id><published>2015-04-13T13:32:00.001-07:00</published><updated>2015-04-13T13:34:31.294-07:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark bite'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='lemon shark'/><title type='text'>Jaws, lemon shark</title><content type='html'>&lt;iframe allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="270" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/O4hifah9UgA" width="480"&gt;&lt;/iframe&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. You can reach us directly at staff@sharkdiver.com.</content><link rel='replies' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/feeds/5176217903761629640/comments/default' title='Post Comments'/><link rel='replies' type='text/html' href='https://www.blogger.com/comment.g?blogID=370711998877298323&amp;postID=5176217903761629640' title='0 Comments'/><link rel='edit' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/5176217903761629640'/><link rel='self' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/5176217903761629640'/><link rel='alternate' type='text/html' href='http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/04/jaws-lemon-shark.html' title='Jaws, lemon shark'/><author><name>Shark Diver</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/107965598445039841723</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='32' height='32' src='//lh5.googleusercontent.com/-acNbaifFSTQ/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAB_A/inqVjDI-1J8/s32-c/photo.jpg'/></author><media:thumbnail xmlns:media='http://search.yahoo.com/mrss/' url='https://img.youtube.com/vi/O4hifah9UgA/default.jpg' height='72' width='72'/><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-7635513399665616395</id><published>2015-04-10T10:15:00.000-07:00</published><updated>2015-04-10T10:15:35.498-07:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='good media for sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark conservation'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark safety'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='cage diving'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='swimming with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark attack'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><title type='text'>Shark Attacks And The Media</title><content type='html'>&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.popsci.com/shark-attacks-are-so-unlikely-so-fascinating"&gt;"Shark Attacks Are So Unlikely, But So Fascinating"&lt;/a&gt; is the title of an article in &lt;a href="http://www.popsci.com/"&gt;Popular Science&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;Wow, a non sensationalistic headline dealing with &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt; attacks. Good job!&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.flmnh.ufl.edu/fish/staff/staff.htm"&gt;George Burgess&lt;/a&gt;,&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt; a shark researcher and curator of the &lt;a class="linkTargets-processed external" href="http://www.flmnh.ufl.edu/fish/sharks/isaf/isaf.htm" target="_blank"&gt;International Shark Attack File&lt;/a&gt; (ISAF) writes a good &lt;a href="http://www.cdc.gov/HomeandRecreationalSafety/Water-Safety/waterinjuries-factsheet.html"&gt;article&lt;/a&gt; on how and why the media covers shark attacks. I don't always agree with him, but think this article gives some good insights into the psychology of shark attacks and how they get covered.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;"Sharks are incredibly unlikely to bite you. They’re even less likely to  kill you. However, we remain fascinated with their ability--and  occasional proclivity--to do just that. With so many things more likely  to harm us, why do we pay such rapt attention when sharks make  headlines?&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;People need to understand more fully that when we enter the sea, it’s  a wilderness experience. We’re eco-tourists and are not owed the right  to be 100% safe. That’s what fascinates us about sharks: There’s an  innate concern in our psyches about not wanting to get eaten. Almost  every other animal on earth has to worry about getting eaten night and  day. As humans, we rarely have that concern. People hold sharks in awe  as one of the rare species that reminds us we’re still potentially part  of a food chain.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;You’re much more likely to be injured or die during your evening run than in a shark attack, but don’t expect to turn on the &lt;a class="linkTargets-processed external" href="http://sharkweekcountdown.com/" target="_blank"&gt;Discovery Channel&lt;/a&gt; and see Sneaker Week. For better or worse, we’re hard-wired to pay  attention to creatures that can eat us--even if they rarely do."&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;I think he hit the nail on the head. In addition to what he mentions, I also believe that for humans to go into the ocean is innately uncomfortable. We are not in our natural environment. There are so many perceived dangers, real or not. We are fascinated by what we may encounter, but also weary of the unknown.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-tsydCekrzRI/U9fYLEqYsoI/AAAAAAAAA_Y/h-MuZMNWzMg/s1600/IMG_5723.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-tsydCekrzRI/U9fYLEqYsoI/AAAAAAAAA_Y/h-MuZMNWzMg/s1600/IMG_5723.jpg" height="236" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Most  people are probably overestimating the chances of getting killed by a  &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt; and who can blame them, with the way we are bombarded with  sensationalistic coverage of anything shark related. In 2014, there were  zero fatal &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt; attacks in the entire US!&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"There wasn’t a single fatality in the entire country last year and only three worldwide." &lt;/i&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.flmnh.ufl.edu/fish/sharks/isaf/2014Summary.html"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;source&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;We always talk about what kills more people than &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt;, but have you ever thought about what kills fewer? What kills humans, but at a rate of fewer than&amp;nbsp; 10-12, or as last year, fewer than 3 annually in the entire world? There may be something, but I haven't come up with an answer yet.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;A lot of people will argue, that there are more fatalities on land, because the number of&amp;nbsp; people who go&amp;nbsp; into the ocean is far lower than the number of people who stay on land and even the people who are going into the water, spend much more time on land as well.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;OK, so let's look at the risks of going into the ocean and what you have to be aware of.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;According to the CDC &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.cdc.gov/HomeandRecreationalSafety/Water-Safety/waterinjuries-factsheet.html"&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"From 2005-2009, there were an average of 3,533  fatal unintentional drownings (non-boating related) annually in the United  States — about ten deaths per day. An additional 347 people died each year from  drowning in boating-related incidents.2"&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Gerry Burgess puts this in perspective. &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;To put that into perspective, &lt;a class="linkTargets-processed external" href="http://www.cdc.gov/HomeandRecreationalSafety/Water-Safety/waterinjuries-factsheet.html" target="_blank"&gt;more people die from drowning&lt;/a&gt; every day in this country than were &lt;a class="linkTargets-processed external" href="http://www.flmnh.ufl.edu/fish/Sharks/Statistics/beachattacks.htm" target="_blank"&gt;killed by sharks in ten years&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;I hope the government of Western Australia is paying attention to this. Their budget for shark mitigation is $22 million. &lt;a href="http://www.perthnow.com.au/news/western-australia/wa-sharkkill-cost-128-million-thats-25000-per-target-shark/story-fnhocxo3-1226957309396"&gt;source&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;nbsp; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;If they would spend that much money on additional lifeguards and life saving equipment instead, they could probably save a lot more lives than with that ill advised shark cull program.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-F9xFjlU2hR0/U_j4t-1qOHI/AAAAAAAABDU/Sg3BMPZreIk/s1600/tiffany-11.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-F9xFjlU2hR0/U_j4t-1qOHI/AAAAAAAABDU/Sg3BMPZreIk/s1600/tiffany-11.JPG" height="347" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;Burgess goes on to explain why the number of annual fatalities has gone up slightly, but the actual rate has gone down.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;When you think of how much time we spend in the water, it’s amazing  how innocuous shark and human interaction is. When the ISAF began in the  1950s, scientists were concerned primarily with shark attacks after  ships and aircraft &lt;a class="linkTargets-processed external" href="http://www.ussindianapolis.org/story.htm" target="_blank"&gt;went down at sea&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;A lot has changed since then. There are a lot more of us on earth  today than there were back then and there will be even more tomorrow.  Aquatic recreation has never been more popular. More people are  kayaking, surfing, diving and paddleboarding.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div class="media media-element-container media-default full-width color-processed"&gt;  &lt;div class="field-credit"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="field-body"&gt;    &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;More time in the water means more time to interface with sharks.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;   &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;It’s partly a generational change. When my parents took a young me to  the beach, my mother would lie on the sand and work on her suntan,  never going in the water. My dad might have gone in once a day to cool  off. Nowadays, if I’m at the beach, I might be boogie boarding or skin  diving. Most of us are spending a lot more hours in the water than did  our parents and our activities are inadvertently provocative. That  creates ample opportunities for sharks and humans to get together.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This article in Popular Science should be mandatory reading for any journalist covering shark related stories. But of course, like Burgess points out, who would watch "Sneaker week". Unfortunately the news is a business and headlines are designed to catch our attention. Like it or not, we are all guilty of it. Like we wrote about &lt;a href="http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/04/shark-trying-to-bite-through-steel-cage.html"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;. What headline are you going to pay attention to. "Shark trying to bite through steel cage!" or "Shark bumps into cage"?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Enjoy your time in the ocean this summer and remember to watch out for rip currents and swim near a lifeguard. If you happen to see a &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt;, consider yourself lucky.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. You can reach us directly at staff@sharkdiver.com.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;</content><link rel='replies' type='application/atom+xml' term='stupid media'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='sensational media'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='guadalupe island'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='safe and sane shark diving'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><title type='text'>Shark trying to bite through steel cage?</title><content type='html'>&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;"Watch terrifying footage of great white shark trying to bite through steel bars of diving cage"&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&amp;nbsp; screams the headline of the &lt;a href="http://www.mirror.co.uk/"&gt;"Daily Mirror"&lt;/a&gt;.&amp;nbsp;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;"Open-mouthed great white shark charges unlucky&amp;nbsp;cameraman" &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;shouts the "&lt;a href="http://nypost.com/"&gt;New York Post&lt;/a&gt;".&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;So what the heck happened?&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;object classid="clsid:D27CDB6E-AE6D-11cf-96B8-444553540000" codebase="http://download.macromedia.com/pub/shockwave/cabs/flash/swflash.cab#version=9,0,47,0" height="370" id="flashObj" It was going after a fish head that was pulled straight over the cage (not a safe practice for a shark diving boat) and ran into the &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving/"&gt;cage&lt;/a&gt; while doing so.&amp;nbsp; Since they don't have a reverse gear and can only swim forward, it looks like it's trying to get into the &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving/"&gt;cage&lt;/a&gt;, when in fact it is just trying to get away.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; by saying &lt;a href="http://www.mirror.co.uk/news/world-news/watch-terrifying-footage-great-white-5478525"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;"The great white shark and many other shark &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a class="inline-link" href="https://www.blogger.com/null"&gt;species&lt;/a&gt; are under threat, so research into their breeding habits can help come  up with scientific solutions to the problems surrounding their possible  extinction.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.mirror.co.uk/news/world-news/watch-terrifying-footage-great-white-5478525"&gt;The main problem is education, most people have grown up thinking sharks are dangerous and scary, and we have Stephen Spielberg's 'Jaws' to thank for that.&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Yes that, and your stupid headline &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;"Watch terrifying footage of great white shark trying to bite through steel bars of diving cage"&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;We at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; specialize in "Safe and Sane" &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving-science-expedition/"&gt;conservation shark diving&lt;/a&gt;. We respect the sharks and try to show them for what they really are. Awesome predators that don't need to be feared, but respected.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;a href="https://scontent-lax.xx.fbcdn.net/hphotos-xpa1/v/t1.0-9/17633_10205972291567271_1076738315426729342_n.jpg?oh=0629663655d3eadf87a802d7afc4b49a&amp;amp;oe=55B3267A" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="217" src="https://scontent-lax.xx.fbcdn.net/hphotos-xpa1/v/t1.0-9/17633_10205972291567271_1076738315426729342_n.jpg?oh=0629663655d3eadf87a802d7afc4b49a&amp;amp;oe=55B3267A" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;If you want to encounter them in their natural environment, come joins us at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving-film-expedition/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt; this fall. You can reach us directly at staff@sharkdiver.com.</content><link rel='replies' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/feeds/2363625253394502825/comments/default' title='Post Comments'/><link rel='replies' type='text/html' href='https://www.blogger.com/comment.g?blogID=370711998877298323&amp;postID=2363625253394502825' title='0 Comments'/><link rel='edit' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/2363625253394502825'/><link rel='self' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/2363625253394502825'/><link rel='alternate' type='text/html' href='http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/04/shark-trying-to-bite-through-steel-cage.html' title='Shark trying to bite through steel cage?'/><author><name>Shark Diver</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/107965598445039841723</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='32' height='32' src='//lh5.googleusercontent.com/-acNbaifFSTQ/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAB_A/inqVjDI-1J8/s32-c/photo.jpg'/></author><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-8091289080841486236</id><published>2015-04-07T11:20:00.001-07:00</published><updated>2015-04-07T17:57:00.354-07:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='dashark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='sea shepherd'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='conservation'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='fiji sharkdive'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='blog'/><title type='text'>How do you get taken seriously as a conservation activist?</title><content type='html'>When writing a blog or a comment on social media, it is easy to get a little rigid in one's stand on an issue or one's view on a group or person. Once our mind is made up, it tends to be difficult for us to change it, or admit that someone we don't like actually did something good.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;People who don't agree with you won't change their mind, unless you have an open mind, are able to see where they are coming from and are able to specifically explain, why you disagree with them. While I can certainly see the passion behind someone opposing, for example &lt;a href="http://www.ocearch.org/"&gt;OCEARCH&lt;/a&gt;, I question whether you can convince someone to see things your way, by just wholesale condemning everything they do. The only people you convince that way, are the ones already agreeing with you.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you speak out against specific things instead, like (OCEARCH) lifting sharks out of the water, the fin damage their tags cause (pictured below) etc. If you explain how those things could be done better,&amp;nbsp; I think you'll have a much better chance to get them to change. Even if they themselves won't change, maybe you'll convince some of their supporters or sponsors and they can make them change.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://news.bbcimg.co.uk/media/images/68347000/jpg/_68347075_findamagephotojyoung.jpg" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img alt="http://news.bbcimg.co.uk/media/images/68347000/jpg/_68347075_findamagephotojyoung.jpg" border="0" src="http://news.bbcimg.co.uk/media/images/68347000/jpg/_68347075_findamagephotojyoung.jpg" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://news.bbcimg.co.uk/media/images/68347000/jpg/_68347075_findamagephotojyoung.jpg"&gt;source&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A great example for doing it right is &lt;a href="https://www.blogger.com/profile/06787762757245289307"&gt;DaShark&lt;/a&gt;. He is certainly a guy with an &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/"&gt;opinion&lt;/a&gt; on things. His view on groups like &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/search?q=Sea+Shepherd&amp;amp;max-results=20&amp;amp;by-date=true"&gt;Sea Shepherd&lt;/a&gt; tend to be mixed to say the least. In his own words &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;" I harbor, to state it mildly, mixed feelings" &lt;/i&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;What makes him different is the fact that he is not rigid in his thinking, he gives credit, when he thinks someone deserves credit, just like he does &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/2015/04/sea-shepherd-vs-pirate-fishermen.html"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/2014/07/wa-shark-cull-submission.html"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Admittedly, it is not easy to have and open mind, and sometimes it hurts to acknowledge that someone is doing something good. DaShark acknowledges that this way &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;Mark this day in your calender! I'm gonna say something positive about the SSCS!&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;i&gt;(And before you ask - yes it did hurt. But what is fair is fair.)"&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;So what does keeping and open mind and working with people instead of against them get you? Well in DaSharks case, a &lt;a href="http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2014/10/shark-conservation-at-its-best.html"&gt;national park&lt;/a&gt;! He is none other than the guy who was instrumental in creating the &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/2014/10/shark-reef-marine-reserve-breaking-news.html"&gt;Shark Reef Marine Reserve&lt;/a&gt; in Fiji, a project that saw the number of fish species present go from around 260 to over 460 in a 10 year span!&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="https://scontent-lax.xx.fbcdn.net/hphotos-xpt1/t31.0-8/10981067_10205720265146768_4471042034064737230_o.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="213" src="https://scontent-lax.xx.fbcdn.net/hphotos-xpt1/t31.0-8/10981067_10205720265146768_4471042034064737230_o.jpg" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;DaShark with his "girls" in the "SRMR"&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Of course it was not just his open mind that got this project accomplished. There was a lot of hard work instead of "slacktivism" involved. In other words, if you really want to change something, you have to do more than just have an opinion and open mind. You have to get off your butt and actually do something.&amp;nbsp; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;You can follow DaShark's blog &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/"&gt;here.&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Cheers,&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Martin Graf&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&amp;nbsp;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds.
