humans for seals? </title><content type='html'>&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Do sharks really mistake humans for seals?&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt; that is the headline of a report in &lt;a href="http://www.smh.com.au/"&gt;"The Sydney Morning Herald"&lt;/a&gt;.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;The article says that&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.smh.com.au/technology/sci-tech/do-sharks-really-mistake-humans-for-seals-researchers-test-mistaken-identity-theory-20150405-1meqwf.html"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;Researchers test 'mistaken identity' theory&lt;b&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;b&gt;&amp;nbsp; &lt;/b&gt;by conducting some studies on sharks in a pool.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.smh.com.au/content/dam/images/1/m/e/s/k/x/image.related.articleLeadwide.620x349.1meqwf.png/1428262179922.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://www.smh.com.au/content/dam/images/1/m/e/s/k/x/image.related.articleLeadwide.620x349.1meqwf.png/1428262179922.jpg" height="225" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;cite&gt;&lt;i&gt;Photo: Taronga Zoo&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/cite&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;cite&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/cite&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;cite&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/cite&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"You can see quite easily how that mistaken identity might come about," Dr Nathan Hart explains.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Look at these images and it's easy to imagine how a shark might mistake a swimmer or surfer for a seal.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;At least that's the premise behind the "mistaken identity" theory that tries to explain why sharks sometimes attack people.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;While the idea seems reasonable, even logical, it has never been tested until now.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;What? Never been tested? Ever heard of Dr. Peter Klimley, Scott Anderson and many others.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.smh.com.au/content/dam/images/1/m/e/s/k/y/image.related.articleLeadwide.620x349.1meqwf.png/1428262179922.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://www.smh.com.au/content/dam/images/1/m/e/s/k/y/image.related.articleLeadwide.620x349.1meqwf.png/1428262179922.jpg" height="223" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;cite&gt;&lt;i&gt;Photo: Taronga Zoo&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/cite&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;At Taronga Zoo, researchers have this month run a series of  experiments to understand what drives a shark to attack by mimicking  what they see and hear underwater.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;With this information, they hope to develop specific shark  repellents, such as making surfboards less attractive with lights; a  feature they'll test on South Africa's white pointer population later  this year.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"We know their visual system isn't as good as ours,"  said lead researcher Nathan Hart, a neuroscientist at the University of  Western Australia.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Sharks are &lt;b&gt;colour blind &lt;/b&gt;but they have very sensitive eyes, making them  good at detecting objects in low contrast. However, they also have poor  spatial acuity, &lt;b&gt;which essentially means their vision is more blurred  than humans&lt;/b&gt;.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Wait, their visual system isn't as good as ours? They are color blind? Their vision is more blurred? I guess Dr. Hart has never heard of &lt;a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samuel_H._Gruber"&gt;Dr. Gruber&lt;/a&gt;'s research&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt; published way back in 1985!&amp;nbsp; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;Thanks to decades of careful,     dedicated work by Samuel Gruber and his co-workers, we now know that &lt;b&gt;many     sharks see in color, too&lt;/b&gt;.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;In a revealing 1985 paper, shark biologist Samuel     Gruber and anatomist Joel Cohen studied the retina of the White Shark.     Gruber and Cohen demonstrated that the Great White retina has both rods and     cones, but at a significantly different ratio from most sharks. The small,     moderately deep-dwelling Spiny Dogfish has a rod-to-cone ratio of about     50:1, while in the larger, more shallow-water Sandbar Shark (Carcharhinus     plumbeus) the rod-to-cone ratio is about 13:1. But in the White Shark, the     rod-to-cone ratio is about 4:1 - roughly the same as in human beings. From     these results, Gruber and Cohen concluded that the White Shark has the     retinal mechanisms necessary for &lt;b&gt;acute, bright-light, color vision&lt;/b&gt;. &lt;a href="http://www.elasmo-research.org/education/white_shark/vision.htm"&gt;source&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;I would expect a researcher to 1. not make a general statement about shark's vision, when different species have very different eyesight and 2. know about the fact that white sharks can see color, which has been known for 30 years now.&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-txZPnlB5kDU/U9wW54NZzUI/AAAAAAAABAQ/LZ0OJ3AAJiM/s1600/Horizon-16.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-txZPnlB5kDU/U9wW54NZzUI/AAAAAAAABAQ/LZ0OJ3AAJiM/s1600/Horizon-16.JPG" height="216" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;I can see you! In color :-)&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Maybe, if Dr. Hart had done a little research on what is already known about &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt;, he would not make statements like these&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"If you now imagine blurring those images, you can see how there'd be  even more similarity between them because the details of the arms and  the legs get hidden," Dr Hart said. "You can see quite easily how that mistaken identity might come about," he said.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;The article states that&amp;nbsp; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;The study forms part of a broader project funded by the Western Australian government to assess shark attack deterrents. &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Well, knowing what kind of "science" the Western Australian Government used to justify their drum line program, I'm not really surprised that they are funding these kinds of researchers.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Link to the article &lt;a href="http://www.smh.com.au/technology/sci-tech/do-sharks-really-mistake-humans-for-seals-researchers-test-mistaken-identity-theory-20150405-1meqwf.html"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt; &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. You can reach us directly at staff@sharkdiver.com.</content><link rel='replies' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/feeds/8393741498334402539/comments/default' title='Post Comments'/><link rel='replies' type='text/html' href='https://www.blogger.com/comment.g?blogID=370711998877298323&amp;postID=8393741498334402539' title='0 Comments'/><link rel='edit' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/8393741498334402539'/><link rel='self' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/8393741498334402539'/><link rel='alternate' type='text/html' href='http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/04/do-sharks-really-mistake-humans-for.html' title='Do sharks really mistake humans for seals? '/><author><name>Shark Diver</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/107965598445039841723</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='32' height='32' src='//lh5.googleusercontent.com/-acNbaifFSTQ/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAB_A/inqVjDI-1J8/s32-c/photo.jpg'/></author><media:thumbnail xmlns:media='http://search.yahoo.com/mrss/' url='http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-txZPnlB5kDU/U9wW54NZzUI/AAAAAAAABAQ/LZ0OJ3AAJiM/s72-c/Horizon-16.JPG' height='72' width='72'/><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-4101105031913955502</id><published>2015-03-27T07:32:00.000-07:00</published><updated>2015-03-27T07:32:08.457-07:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='projects abroad'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='swimming with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='conservation'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='volunteer with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='environment'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><title type='text'>Awesome volunteer opportunity for 16-19 year olds!</title><content type='html'>We just wrote that our friends at &lt;a href="http://www.projects-abroad.co.uk/"&gt;Projects Abroad&lt;/a&gt; looking for a &lt;a href="http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/03/looking-for-summer-job-but-would-prefer.html"&gt;Volunteer Coordinator&lt;/a&gt;. Since they need a volunteer coordinator, they obviously also need volunteers and are looking for 16-19 year old adventurers, who would like to live and work in Cambodia for a couple of weeks. The volunteers will be able to get SCUBA certified and help out with local conservation and community projects. What an awesome opportunity!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.projects-abroad.co.uk/_photos/_global/photo-galleries/uk/cambodia/_global/large/khmer-project.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://www.projects-abroad.co.uk/_photos/_global/photo-galleries/uk/cambodia/_global/large/khmer-project.jpg" height="300" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here is all the info you from their &lt;a href="http://www.projects-abroad.co.uk/volunteer-projects/short-term-specials/conservation-and-environment/conservation-and-community/cambodia/#overview|project-overview"&gt;website&lt;/a&gt;. &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt;2 Week Summer Program&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table border="0" cellspacing="0" class="hs"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: justify;"&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;Sunday June 21st 2015 - Saturday July 4th 2015&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;Sunday July 12th 2015 - Saturday July 25th 2015&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;Sunday August 2nd 2015 - Saturday August 15th 2015&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt;2 Week Winter Program&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;Sunday December 6th 2015 - Saturday December 19th 2015&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;div class="country-facts-box"&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;Placement location: &lt;/b&gt;Koh Sdach&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;Types of placement: &lt;/b&gt;Diving and Conservation&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;Accommodation: &lt;/b&gt;Shared Dorms &lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;Age Requirements: &lt;/b&gt;16-19 years old&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Volunteers  joining our Conservation &amp;amp; Community project in Cambodia will  travel to the tropical island of Koh Sdach where you will live in a  house over the water, in the local village. The facilities are basic,  but you will become part of this tiny island community, learn to dive  and take part in conservation and community projects.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a class="photo-zoom right-align cboxElement" href="http://www.projects-abroad.co.uk/_photos/volunteer-projects/short-term-specials/conservation-and-community-in-cambodia/conservation-in-cambodia.1200.jpg" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;" title="Conservation &amp;amp; Community in Cambodia"&gt;&lt;img alt="Conservation &amp;amp; Community in Cambodia" class="right-align" src="http://www.projects-abroad.co.uk/_photos/volunteer-projects/short-term-specials/conservation-and-community-in-cambodia/conservation-in-cambodia.jpg" height="300" title="Conservation &amp;amp; Community in Cambodia" width="400" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;During your  stay you will complete an internationally recognised PADI Open Water  course to qualify you to dive. In the initial stages when you're in  shallow water, you will learn how to breathe, clear your mask and  equalise pressure. You will also become familiar with the buddy system  and underwater sign language.&lt;br /&gt;Once you have qualified, you will  take part in clean-up salvage dives and seahorse search dives. You will  also take part in a jungle trek and help with a beach clean-up. You will  also join a practical community project, which may be clearing land and  building a children's playground, helping to build an incinerator or an  aquaculture pond.&lt;br /&gt;During the two weeks you may also have chance  to join a village fun day - playing games and running fun water-based  activities with the village children.&lt;br /&gt;This placement is fully  researched, safety audited and risk assessed in accordance with the  British Standard BS8848 for the Adventure Travel Sector.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;For more information, click &lt;a href="http://www.projects-abroad.co.uk/volunteer-projects/short-term-specials/conservation-and-environment/conservation-and-community/cambodia/#overview|project-overview"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;, to apply, click &lt;a href="http://www.projects-abroad.co.uk/volunteer-projects/short-term-specials/conservation-and-environment/conservation-and-community/cambodia/#overview|project-overview"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="https://www.facebook.com/gapyears/photos_stream"&gt;Projects Abroad&lt;/a&gt; is an awesome organization that is helping people and the environment  around the world. I have had the pleasure of working alongside them in &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/bull-shark-diving-fiji/"&gt;Fiji &lt;/a&gt;and  can attest to the fact, that the work feels more like an adventure than working. Here is your opportunity to have an  adventure and the knowledge that you made a difference.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I hope you'll get to help them out and have an awesome time!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO Shark Diver&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='projects abroad'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='cage diving'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='swimming with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='marine conservation'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='volunteer with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='summer job'/><title type='text'>Looking for a summer job, but would prefer an adventure?</title><content type='html'>Summer is approaching fast and if you are looking for a job, but would prefer an adventure, have we found an opportunity for you!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="https://scontent.xx.fbcdn.net/hphotos-xpf1/v/t1.0-9/10931408_10152939569006068_5882875916571581201_n.png?oh=cb7ea588c7f4ea67b6e43906ef4e7ca1&amp;amp;oe=5571A08A" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="320" src="https://scontent.xx.fbcdn.net/hphotos-xpf1/v/t1.0-9/10931408_10152939569006068_5882875916571581201_n.png?oh=cb7ea588c7f4ea67b6e43906ef4e7ca1&amp;amp;oe=5571A08A" width="319" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Our friends at &lt;a href="http://www.projects-abroad.co.uk/"&gt;Projects Abroad&lt;/a&gt; are looking for a Volunteer Coordinator. &lt;a href="https://www.facebook.com/gapyears/photos_stream"&gt;Projects Abroad&lt;/a&gt; is an awesome organization that is helping people and the environment around the world. I have had the pleasure of working alongside them in &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/bull-shark-diving-fiji/"&gt;Fiji &lt;/a&gt;and can attest to the fact, that the work is more of an adventure than a job. Here is your opportunity to have a summer job that offers you adventure and the knowledge that you made a difference.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="https://scontent.xx.fbcdn.net/hphotos-xpa1/v/t1.0-9/10404344_10154915826280507_4535032939583699000_n.jpg?oh=6e96e63e589070f40e6ca5ddb71bbe30&amp;amp;oe=55A95F6D" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="240" src="https://scontent.xx.fbcdn.net/hphotos-xpa1/v/t1.0-9/10404344_10154915826280507_4535032939583699000_n.jpg?oh=6e96e63e589070f40e6ca5ddb71bbe30&amp;amp;oe=55A95F6D" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is from their &lt;a href="http://www.projects-abroad.co.uk/about-us/jobs-with-projects-abroad/short-term-special-coordinator/"&gt;website&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table border="0"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td valign="top" width="25%"&gt;&lt;b&gt;Job title &lt;/b&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td width="75%"&gt;Volunteer Coordinator – Short-term Specials &lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td valign="top"&gt;&lt;b&gt;Location&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;To be confirmed, however should include: Cambodia, India, Nepal, Sri Lanka and Tanzania. &lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td valign="top"&gt;&lt;b&gt;Contract&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;We  are recruiting Volunteer Coordinators for our Short-term Specials in  several destinations. You will usually be employed on a 2 or 3 month  contract starting in June 2015. An offer of employment is dependent upon  receipt of satisfactory references, a criminal record check and  personal interview.&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td valign="top"&gt;&lt;b&gt;Job description&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;As  a Volunteer Coordinator for our Short-term Specials you will support  our overseas teams of staff headed by the Country Director. We recruit  Short-term Special volunteers from June to August each summer. &lt;b&gt;Job role:&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;Working  alongside our team of local staff, you will be responsible for making  each new arrival feel welcome and secure in their new environment.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;You  will complete inductions with the new volunteers, introducing them to  their host family and work project and explaining cultural differences  and expectations of their project.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;You will help maintain effective communication between the destination office, the volunteers and the UK office.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;•  You will support the Short-term Special volunteers throughout their  time with Projects Abroad. This will include supervising them at their  placement and during cultural activities.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;The job is busy; it  will involve some out-of-office hours work and can be physically  demanding. You should be prepared to be on call on any day during your  time overseas.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;b&gt;Requirements; you should be:&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;A graduate&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Fluent in English, both spoken and written&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Physically fit&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Computer literate, (Microsoft Office, databases) &lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Mature in attitude and outlook&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Able to remain calm and efficient under pressure &lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Flexible and able to take direction and accept feedback &lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Friendly and personable with customer service skills, you must respond well to others&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Enthusiastic to work in a different culture and relish the opportunity to work in a challenging environment&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Experience in volunteering &lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Experience in living overseas.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Additional languages, especially French, Spanish, German or Japanese will be an advantage.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td valign="top"&gt;&lt;b&gt;Salary &amp;amp; benefits&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;Projects  Abroad pays a good local salary, international flights, comprehensive  travel and health insurance, board and lodging as well as agreed  day-to-day work-related expenses.&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td valign="top"&gt;&lt;b&gt;To apply&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;Email your CV and a covering letter to: &lt;a href="mailto:workforus@projects-abroad.net"&gt;workforus@projects-abroad.net.&lt;/a&gt; Please state on your application that you are applying for a Short-term Special Coordinator position.&lt;br /&gt;Unsuccessful applicants will not be contacted.&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Good luck with your application and have an awesome summer!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO Shark Diver&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds.
